9 COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 525, L.D. 715, "An Act To Make Certain 
10 Appropriations and Allocations and Changing Certain Provisions of the Law Necessary to 
11 the Proper Operations of State Government" 
12 Amend the bill by striking out the title and substituting the following: 
13 'An Act Making Unified Appropriations and Allocations for the Expenditures of State 
14 Government, General Fund and Other Funds and Changing Certain Provisions of the 
15 Law Necessary to the Proper Operations of State Government for the Fiscal Years 
16 Ending June 30, 2022 and June 30, 2023' 
17 Amend the bill by inserting before enacting clause the following: 
18 'Emergency preamble. Whereas, acts and resolves of the Legislature do not 
19 become effective until 90 days after adjournment unless enacted as emergencies; and 
20 Whereas, the 90-day period may not terminate until after the beginning of the next 
21 fiscal year; and 
22 Whereas, certain obligations and expenses incident to the operation of state 
23 departments and institutions will become due and payable immediately; and 
24 Whereas, in the judgment of the Legislature, these facts create an emergency within 
25 the meaning of the Constitution of Maine and require the following legislation as 
26 immediately necessary for the preservation of the public peace, health and safety; now, 
27 therefore,' 
28 Amend the bill by striking out everything after the enacting clause and inserting the 
29 following: 
30 'PART A 
31 Sec. A-1. Appropriations and allocations. The following appropriations and 
32 allocations are made. 
33 ADMINISTRATIVE AND FINANCIAL SERVICES, DEPARTMENT OF

Sec. C-8. Authorization of payments. If the State's continued obligation for any 
individual component contained in those sections of this Part that set the total cost of 
funding public education from kindergarten to grade 12 and the local and state 
contributions for that purpose exceeds the level of funding provided for that component, 
any unexpended balances occurring in other programs may be applied to avoid proration 
of payments for any individual component. Any unexpended balances from this Part may 
not lapse but must be carried forward for the same purpose. 
Sec. C-9. Limit of State's obligation. Those sections of this Part that set the total 
cost of funding public education from kindergarten to grade 12 and the local and state 
contributions for that purpose may not be construed to require the State to provide payments 
that exceed the appropriation of funds for general purpose aid for local schools for the fiscal 
year beginning July 1, 2021 and ending June 30, 2022.

Sec. E-1. Emergency rule-making authority; health and human services 
matters. The Department of Health and Human Services is authorized to adopt 
emergency rules under the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 5, sections 8054 and 8073 as 
necessary to implement those provisions of this Act over which the department has subject 
matter jurisdiction for which specific authority has not been provided in any other Part of 
this Act without the necessity of demonstrating that immediate adoption is necessary to 
avoid a threat to public health, safety or general welfare. 
PARTF 
Sec. F-1. 30-A MRSA §5681, sub-§5, as amended by PL 2019, c. 343, Pt. H, §1, 
is further amended to read: 
5. Transfers to funds. No later than the 10th day of each month, the State Controller . 
shall transfer to the Local Government Fund 5% of the receipts during the previous month 
from the taxes imposed under Title 36, Parts 3 and 8, and Title 36, section 2552, subsection 
1, paragraphs A to F and L, and credited to the General Fund without any reduction, except 
that for fiscal years 2015-16, 2016-17, 2017-18 and 2018-19 the amount transferred is 2%, 
for fiscal year 2019-20 the amount transferred is 3% and for fiscal year years 2020-2t 
2021-22, and 2022-23, the amount transferred is 3.75% of the receipts during the previous 
month from the taxes imposed under Title 36, Parts 3 and 8, and Title 36, section 2552, 
subsection 1, paragraphs A to F and L, and credited to the General Fund without any 
reduction, and except that the postage, state cost allocation program and programming costs 
of administering state-municipal revenue sharing may be paid by the Local Government 
Fund. A percentage share of the amounts transferred to the Local Government Fund each 
month must be transferred to the Disproportionate Tax Burden Fund and distributed 
pursuant to subsection 4-B as follows: 
C. For months beginning on or after July 1, 2009 but before July 1, 2010, 15%; 
I D. For months beginning on or after July 1, 2010 but before July 1, 2011, 16%; 
E. For months beginning on or after July 1, 2011 but before July 1, 2012, 17%; 
F. For months beginning on or after July 1, 2012 but before July 1, 2013, 18%; 
G. For months beginning on or after July 1, 2013 but before July 1, 2014, 19%; and 
H. For months beginning on or after July 1, 2014, 20%.

budget document submitted to the Legislature by the Governor on January 8, 2021.

Sec. H-1. Transfer of funds. Notwithstanding any provision of law to the contrary, 
the State Controller shall transfer to the unappropriated surplus of the General Fund

PARTI 
Sec. 1-1. Attrition savings. Notwithstanding any provision of law to the contrary, 
the attrition rate for the 2022-2023 biennium is 5% for judicial branch and executive branch 
departments and agencies only. The attrition rate for subsequent biennia is 1.6%. 
Sec. 1-2. Calculation and transfer; attrition savings. The State Budget Officer 
shall calculate the amount of the savings in Part A that applies against each General Fund 
account for all executive branch departments and agencies statewide and shall transfer the 
amounts by financial order upon the approval of the Governor. These transfers are 
considered adjustments to appropriations in fiscal years 2021-22 and 2022-23. The State 
Budget Officer shall submit to the Joint Standing Committee on Appropriations and 
Financial Affairs a report of the transferred amounts no later than October 1, 2021. 
Sec. 1-3. Appropriations and allocations. The following appropriations and 
allocations are made.

from 1.6% to 5% for fiscal years 2021-22 and 2022-23.

5 SUMMARY 
6 PART A 
7 This Part makes appropriations and allocations offunds for the 2022-2023 biennium. 
8 PART B 
9 This Part makes appropriations and allocations of funds for approved reclassifications 
10 and range changes. 
11 PART C 
12 This Part does the following. 
13 I. It establishes the total cost of education from kindergarten to grade 12, the state 
14 contribution, the annual target state share percentage and the mill expectation for the local 
15 contribution for fiscal year 2021-22. 
16 2. It provides a one-year change to the State's essential programs and services 
17 education funding model in order to recognize the pecline in student enrollment for the . 
18 year prior to funding and, due to the unusual nature of the decline, the inability of school 
19 administrative units to reduce their costs accordingly. 
20 PARTD 
21 This Part makes adjustments to the appropriations and allocations in Part A. 
22 PARTE 
23 This Part authorizes the Department of Health and Human Services to adopt emergency 
24 rules to implement any provisions of this Act over which the department has specific 
25 authority that has not been addressed by some other Part of the Act without the necessity 
26 of demonstrating that immediate adoption is necessary to avoid a threat to public health, 
27 safety or welfare. 
28 This Part is similar to Part WW of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
29 PARTF 
30 This Part sets the transfer to the Local Government Fund at 3. 7 5% in fiscal years 2021-
31 22 and 2022-23. 
32 This Part is similar to Part G of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
33 PARTG 
34 This Part continues authorization for each individual tax expenditure provided by 
35 statute. 
36 This Part is similar to Part R of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
37 PARTH 
Page 290 -130LR0432(02)

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 525, L.D. 715

4 This Part is similar to Part J of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
5 PART I 
6 · This Part changes the attrition rate for the 2022-2023 biennium from 1.6% to 5% for 
7 judicial branch and executive branch departments and agencies. 
8 This Part is similar to Part P of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
9 PARTJ 
10 This Part continues the voluntary employee incentive program through the 2022-2023 
11 biennium. 
12 This Part is similar to Part Q of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
13 PARTK 
14 This Part directs the Maine Municipal Bond Bank to transfer to the General Fund 
15 $40,000,000, $20,000,000 in each fiscal year of the biennium, from the Liquor Operation 
16 Revenue Fund. These revenues are in excess of the amount required for debt payments and 
17 previously authorized transfers. 
18 This Part is similar to Part S of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
19 PART L 
20 This Part removes the Education in the Unorganized Territory account within the 
21 Department of Education from the list of accounts authorized to carry unexpended General 
22 Fund Personal Services balances and transfers the accumulated balance to the 
23 unappropriated surplus of the General Fund. 
24 This Part i_s similar to Part HH of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
25 PARTM 
26 This Part updates the base year for the hospital tax. 
27 This Part is similar to Part 00 of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
28 PARTN 
29 This Part lapses $3,000,000 of the unencumbered balance forward of the Department 
30 of Health and Human Services, General Assistance -Reimbursement to Cities and Towns, 
31 General Fund carrying account to the unappropriated surplus of the General Fund in fiscal 
32 year 2021-22. 
33 This Part is similar to Part BBB of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget. 
34 PARTO 
35 This Part lapses $5,000,000 of the unencumbered balance forward of the Department 
36 of Health and Human Services, Temporary Assistance for Needy Families, General Fund 
37 account to the General Fund in fiscal year 2021-22. 
38 This Part is similar to Part CCC of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget.

18 PARTS 
19 This Part transfers $32,000,000 from Other Special Revenue Funds to the 
20 unappropriated surplus of the General Fund by June 30, 2022 and reverses that transfer, 
21 with interest, on July 1, 2022. 
22 PARTT 
23 This Part delays the beginning of the Fiscal Stability Program, which requires a 
24 biennial budget submitted by the Governor to include a General Fund appropriation of 18% 
25 in excess of the Department of Inland Fisheries and Wildlife's requested budget, until the 
26 2024-2025 biennium. 
27 This Part is similar to Part GGG of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial 
28 budget. 
29 PARTU 
30 This Part authorizes the State Court Administrator to increase the salaries of the State's 
31 chief justices, Chief Judge, Deputy Chief Judge, associate justices and associate judges by 
32 3% in each of fiscal years 2021-22 and 2022-23, effective July 1, 2021 and July 1, 2022. 
33 This Part is similar to Part III of the Governor's proposed 2022-2023 biennial budget.
